     <p>The <b>University of Arizona</b> (also referred to as <b>UA</b> (spoken as <b>U of A</b>), or <b>Arizona</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Land-grant_university" title="Land-grant university">land-grant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Space_grant_colleges" title="Space grant colleges" class="mw-redirect">space-grant</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> institution of higher education and research located in <a href="/wiki/Tucson,_Arizona" title="Tucson, Arizona">Tucson, Arizona</a>, United States. The University of Arizona was the first university in the state of <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, founded in 1885 (twenty-seven years before the Arizona Territory achieved statehood). The university includes the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Arizona College of Medicine">University of Arizona College of Medicine</a> which is one of three medical schools and the only <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Medicine" title="Doctor of Medicine">MD</a> granting medical school in Arizona. As of Fall 2010, total enrollment was 39,086 students.<sup id="cite_ref-Fact_Book_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fact_Book-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Arizona is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Board_of_Regents" title="Arizona Board of Regents">Arizona Board of Regents</a>. The mission of the University of Arizona is, &quot;To discover, educate, serve, and inspire.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-UA_Mission_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UA_Mission-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Arizona is one of the elected members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (an organization of North America's premier research institutions) and is the only representative from the state of Arizona to this group.</p> 
     <p>Known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats" title="Arizona Wildcats">Arizona Wildcats</a></i> (often shortened to &quot;'Cats&quot;), the athletic teams are members of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a> in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>. UA athletes have won national titles in several sports, most notably men's basketball, baseball, and softball. The official colors of the university and its athletic teams are Cardinal Red and Navy Blue.</p>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Main_(U_of_Arizona).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Old_Main_%28U_of_Arizona%29.jpg/200px-Old_Main_%28U_of_Arizona%29.jpg" width="200" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Old_Main_%28U_of_Arizona%29.jpg/300px-Old_Main_%28U_of_Arizona%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Old_Main_%28U_of_Arizona%29.jpg/400px-Old_Main_%28U_of_Arizona%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Old_Main_(U_of_Arizona).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Old Main, the oldest building on the University of Arizona campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Arizona was approved by the Arizona Territory's &quot;<a href="/wiki/Thieving_Thirteenth" title="Thieving Thirteenth" class="mw-redirect">Thieving Thirteenth</a>&quot; Legislature in 1885. The city of Tucson had hoped to receive the appropriation for the territory's mental hospital, which carried a $100,000 allocation instead of the $25,000 allotted to the territory's only university (Arizona State University was also chartered in 1885, but at the time it was created as Arizona's <a href="/wiki/Normal_school" title="Normal school">normal school</a>, and not a university). <a href="/wiki/Tucson" title="Tucson" class="mw-redirect">Tucson</a>'s contingent of legislators was delayed in reaching <a href="/wiki/Prescott,_Arizona" title="Prescott, Arizona">Prescott</a> due to flooding on the <a href="/wiki/Salt_River_(Arizona)" title="Salt River (Arizona)">Salt River</a> and by the time they arrived back-room deals allocating the most desirable territorial institutions had already been made.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:412px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/81/OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg/410px-OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg" width="410" height="238" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/81/OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg/615px-OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/81/OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:OldMain_UofA_1889.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Old Main in 1889
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Tucson was largely disappointed at receiving what was viewed as an inferior prize. With no parties willing to step forth and provide land for the new institution, the citizens of Tucson prepared to return the money to the Territorial Legislature until two gamblers and a saloon keeper decided to donate the land necessary to build the school. Classes met for the first time in 1891 with 32 students in Old Main, the first building constructed on the 40 acre<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> campus, and still in use to this day.<sup id="cite_ref-History_3_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_3-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Because there were no high schools in Arizona Territory, the University maintained separate preparatory classes for the first 23 years of operation.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Wildcat_Family_Statue,_University_of_Arizona.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Wildcat_Family_Statue%2C_University_of_Arizona.jpg/220px-Wildcat_Family_Statue%2C_University_of_Arizona.jpg" width="220" height="281" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Wildcat_Family_Statue%2C_University_of_Arizona.jpg/330px-Wildcat_Family_Statue%2C_University_of_Arizona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Wildcat_Family_Statue%2C_University_of_Arizona.jpg/440px-Wildcat_Family_Statue%2C_University_of_Arizona.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Wildcat_Family_Statue,_University_of_Arizona.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Wildcat Family Statue
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University of Arizona offers 334 fields of study leading to bachelor's, master's, doctoral, and professional degrees. Academic departments and programs are organized into colleges and schools. The university maintains a current list of colleges and schools at <a rel="nofollow" class="external free" href="http://www.arizona.edu/index/colleges.php">http://www.arizona.edu/index/colleges.php</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Arizona is the only remaining <a href="/wiki/Pac-12" title="Pac-12" class="mw-redirect">Pac-12</a> conference school to not award plus and minus grades for courses. Currently, grades are given on a strict 4-point scale with &quot;A&quot; worth 4, &quot;B&quot; worth 3, &quot;C&quot; worth 2, &quot;D&quot; worth 1 and &quot;E&quot; worth zero points. In 2004, there were discussions with students and faculty that may lead the UA towards eventual usage of the plus-minus grading system in future years.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the university still uses the 4-points scale.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings">Rankings</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Rankings">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>In 2012, U.S. News &amp; World Report ranked the University of Arizona as the 120th best national university<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> in the United States. In 2013, the Eller MBA program was ranked 44th by U.S. News &amp; World Report, which ranked the Entrepreneurship specialization #11 and the MIS specialization #4. The Council for Aid to Education ranked the UA 12th among public universities and 24th overall in financial support and gifts.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2013)">not in citation given</span></a></i>]</sup> <i>Campaign Arizona</i>, an effort to raise over $1 billion USD for the school, exceeded that goal by $200 million a year earlier than projected.<sup id="cite_ref-UA_Highlights_2004-5_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UA_Highlights_2004-5-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/James_E._Rogers_College_of_Law" title="James E. Rogers College of Law">James E. Rogers College of Law</a> was ranked 38th nationally and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona_College_of_Medicine" title="University of Arizona College of Medicine">University of Arizona College of Medicine</a> was ranked 44th nationally in <a href="/wiki/Primary_care" title="Primary care">primary care</a> by U.S. News &amp; World Report in for 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> The College of Medicine was also ranked No. 7 among the nation's medical schools for Hispanic students, according to Hispanic Business Magazine.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The Systems and <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Engineering" title="Industrial Engineering" class="mw-redirect">Industrial Engineering</a> (SIE) Department is ranked 10th in the 'America's Best Graduate Schools 2009' by US News and World Report. The <a href="/wiki/Applied_mathematics" title="Applied mathematics">applied mathematics</a> program at UA is ranked 17th nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report (2011).<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Analytical_chemistry" title="Analytical chemistry">analytical chemistry</a> program at UA is ranked 6th nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report (2010).<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Agricultural and Biosystems Engineering (ABE) Department is ranked 16th nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report (2012).<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">Geology</a> program is ranked 1st nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Doctor_of_Pharmacy" title="Doctor of Pharmacy">Doctor of Pharmacy</a> program at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona_College_of_Pharmacy" title="University of Arizona College of Pharmacy">University of Arizona College of Pharmacy</a> is ranked 9th nationally by U.S. News &amp; World Report in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The Photography program is ranked 9th nationally, also by U.S. News &amp; World Report in 2008. The philosophy program is ranked 13th nationally by the <a href="/wiki/Philosophical_Gourmet_Report" title="Philosophical Gourmet Report">Philosophical Gourmet Report</a>, and No. 46 in Political Science. Internationally, the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked University of Arizona 95th in the world and the 2011 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> ranked this university 183rd. In its May 2009 issue, <i><a href="/wiki/Playboy" title="Playboy">Playboy</a></i> magazine ranked UA the fifth best party school in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the College of Architecture and Landscape Architecture's (CALA) undergraduate program in architecture was ranked 12th in the nation for all universities, public and private, as reported in Design Intelligence.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=School_of_Middle_Eastern_and_North_African_Studies&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="School of Middle Eastern and North African Studies (page does not exist)">School of Middle Eastern and North African Studies</a><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> at the University of Arizona is one of the most highly ranked area studies programs focusing on the Middle East in the United States. In addition to offering language training in <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic" class="mw-redirect">Arabic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hebrew" title="Hebrew" class="mw-redirect">Hebrew</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_language" title="Turkish language">Turkish</a> (both Modern and <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Turkish_language" title="Ottoman Turkish language">Ottoman</a>), it is collocated with the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East_Studies_Association" title="Middle East Studies Association" class="mw-redirect">Middle East Studies Association</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a>]</span></h3>

     <p>The UA admitted 75% of applicants in the 2012-2013 academic year and is considered a &quot;selective&quot; university by <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_and_World_Report" title="U.S. News and World Report" class="mw-redirect">U.S. News and World Report</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> In the 2012-2013 academic year, 82 freshman students were <a href="/wiki/National_Merit_Scholarship" title="National Merit Scholarship" class="mw-redirect">National Merit Scholars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Student_Data_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Student_Data-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UA students hail from all states in the U.S. While nearly 72% of students are from <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, nearly 10% are from California, followed by a significant student presence from <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>, Texas, <a href="/wiki/Washington_(state)" title="Washington (state)">Washington</a>, and New York (2007).<sup id="cite_ref-Fact_Book_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fact_Book-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The UA has over 2,200 international students representing 122 countries. International students comprise approximately 6% of the total enrollment at UA.<sup id="cite_ref-Fact_Book_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fact_Book-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tuition">Tuition</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Tuition">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Tuition at the University of Arizona is the second lowest in Arizona for 4 year universities with tuition at $9286 for undergraduate residents.<sup id="cite_ref-arizona.edu_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arizona.edu-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> As in other states, the cost of tuition has been rising due to the decrease in government support.<sup id="cite_ref-arizona.edu_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arizona.edu-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> In the past year, the university has experienced rises in tuition of 4.7%,<sup id="cite_ref-arizona.edu_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arizona.edu-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> but will not be experiencing any increases for residents in the 2012–2013 academic year.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_College">Honors College</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Honors College">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Arizona Honors College provides a program for over 3,000 students that creates a smaller community feel, like that of a liberal arts college, within a large, research institution. It started in 1962 with an acceptance of seventy-five students and has since grown to 3,316 in the academic year 2010–2011 <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.honors.arizona.edu">[4]</a>. The main offices for the University of Arizona Honors College are located near Park Ave. and 2nd Street, near the Harvill Lecture Hall building. These offices are known as the Slonaker House.</p> 
     <p>The University of Arizona Honors College is in affiliation with the University of Arizona and is headed by Dean Dr. Patricia MacCorquodale and Associate Dean Dr. Laura Berry. Under the Dean and Vice Dean are the offices of the Academic Advising Coordinator, Director of Nationally Competitive Scholarships, Director of Recruitment and Outreach, Director of Development, Program Coordinator for Career and Development and Community Engagement, Honors Professors, and Honors advisors.</p> 
     <p>The University of Arizona Honors College has a strong first-year program for its students that includes common reading materials and Colloquium/Paladin classes everyone must take as a freshman. The overall requirements for the program entail that each honors student must complete 30 credit hours of honors credit by graduation time and maintain a cumulative GPA of 3.5. To complete these credit hours, students may take courses specifically designated as honors at the University of Arizona or may turn a regular course into an <a href="/wiki/Honors_course" title="Honors course" class="mw-redirect">honors course</a> through the use of an honors contract. Certain restrictions apply. In addition, they must collaborate with a <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(teaching_staff)" title="Faculty (teaching staff)" class="mw-redirect">faculty</a> member and write an honors thesis before graduating with honors from the University of Arizona.</p> 
     <p>The University of Arizona Honors College provides two on-campus <a href="/wiki/Dorms" title="Dorms" class="mw-redirect">dorms</a> for their students, Yuma Hall and &Aacute;rbol de la Vida. Yuma houses 184 men and women <sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> and is located near the Slonaker House on East North Campus Drive by the Maricopa Residence Hall. &Aacute;rbol de la Vida houses 719 men and women and is situated on the edge of campus on 6th street and Tyndall Avenue near the Park Student Union and the <a href="/wiki/Dorm" title="Dorm" class="mw-redirect">dorm</a>, Arizona Sonora. The two halls offer different community feels for their students. Yuma presents a close-knit, small community while &Aacute;rbol de la Vida provides a larger community of honors students with a newer, more modern living experience. Yuma was renovated and turned into an honors <a href="/wiki/Dorm" title="Dorm" class="mw-redirect">dorm</a> in 1988, whereas &Aacute;rbol de la Vida first opened to students in the Fall of 2011 <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.honors.arizona.edu">[5]</a>.</p> 
     <p>There are additional resources available to honors students in the University of Arizona Honors College. Such resources include: longer library check-out dates, cheaper printing options at the Slonaker House, priority registration, additional honors advising, smaller class sizes taught by Honors faculty, clubs and organizations specifically available to only honors students such as the Honors Student Council and the Honors College Ambassadors, and additional scholarship opportunities. However, there is also a fee for participating in honors and an additional honors thesis is required of its students before graduation <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://www.honors.arizona.edu">[6]</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Arizona is classified as a <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Classification_of_Institutions_of_Higher_Education" title="Carnegie Classification of Institutions of Higher Education">Carnegie Foundation</a> &quot;RU/VH: Research Universities (very high research activity)&quot; university (formerly &quot;Research 1&quot; university). The university receives more than $600 million USD annually in research funding, generating around two thirds of the research dollars in the Arizona university system,<sup id="cite_ref-Highlights_and_rankings_16_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highlights_and_rankings_16-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> 26th highest in the U.S. (including public and private institutions).<sup id="cite_ref-uaadvancement_1_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uaadvancement_1-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has an endowment of $480.2 million USD as of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-2010_NACUBO_Endowment_Study_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2010_NACUBO_Endowment_Study-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The U of A is awarded more <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> grants for space exploration than any other university nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The UA was awarded over $325 million USD for its <a href="/wiki/Lunar_and_Planetary_Laboratory" title="Lunar and Planetary Laboratory">Lunar and Planetary Laboratory</a> (LPL) to lead <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(spacecraft)" title="Phoenix (spacecraft)">NASA's 2007–08 mission to Mars</a> to explore the Martian Arctic. The LPL's work in the <a href="/wiki/Cassini-Huygens" title="Cassini-Huygens" class="mw-redirect">Cassini</a> spacecraft orbit around <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a> is larger than that of any other university globally. The U of A laboratory designed and operated the atmospheric radiation investigations and imaging on the probe.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> The UA operates the <a href="/wiki/HiRISE" title="HiRISE">HiRISE</a> camera, a part of the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter">Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter</a>. UA receives more <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> grants annually than the next nine top NASA-<a href="/wiki/Jet_Propulsion_Laboratory" title="Jet Propulsion Laboratory">Jet Propulsion Laboratory</a>-funded universities combined.<sup id="cite_ref-UA_Highlights_2004-5_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UA_Highlights_2004-5-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2011, the UA's Lunar and Planetary Laboratory is actively involved in five spacecraft missions: Cassini; the Phoenix Mars Lander; the HiRISE camera orbiting Mars; the MESSENGER mission to Mercury and OSIRIS-REx, the first U.S. sample return mission to an asteroid, which was just selected by NASA.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> UA students have been selected as <a href="/wiki/Harry_S._Truman_Scholarship" title="Harry S. Truman Scholarship">Truman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholarship" title="Rhodes Scholarship">Rhodes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barry_M._Goldwater_Scholarship" title="Barry M. Goldwater Scholarship">Goldwater</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fulbright_Scholarship" title="Fulbright Scholarship" class="mw-redirect">Fulbright</a> Scholars.<sup id="cite_ref-Highlights_and_rankings_17_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highlights_and_rankings_17-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i>The Chronicle of Higher Education</i>, UA is among the top 25 producers of Fulbright awards in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-UA_Highlights_2004-5_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UA_Highlights_2004-5-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>UA is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_for_Research_in_Astronomy" title="Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy">Association of Universities for Research in Astronomy</a>, a consortium of institutions pursuing research in astronomy. The association operates observatories and <a href="/wiki/Telescopes" title="Telescopes" class="mw-redirect">telescopes</a>, notably <a href="/wiki/Kitt_Peak_National_Observatory" title="Kitt Peak National Observatory">Kitt Peak National Observatory</a> located just outside of Tucson. UA is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, and the sole representative from Arizona to this group. Led by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Angel" title="Roger Angel">Roger Angel</a>, researchers in the <a href="/wiki/Steward_Observatory" title="Steward Observatory">Steward Observatory</a> Mirror Lab at UA are working in concert to build the world's most advanced telescope. Known as the <a href="/wiki/Giant_Magellan_Telescope" title="Giant Magellan Telescope">Giant Magellan Telescope</a>, the instrument will produce images 10 times sharper than those from the Earth-orbiting <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Telescope" title="Hubble Telescope" class="mw-redirect">Hubble Telescope</a>. The telescope is set to be completed in 2016 at a cost of $500 million USD. Researchers from at least nine institutions are working to secure the funding for the project. The telescope will include seven 18-ton mirrors capable of providing clear images of <a href="/wiki/Volcanoes" title="Volcanoes" class="mw-redirect">volcanoes</a> and riverbeds on <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> and mountains on the moon at a rate 40 times faster than the world's current large telescopes. The mirrors of the Giant Magellan Telescope will be built at the U of A and transported to a permanent mountaintop site in the <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chilean</a> <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">Andes</a> where the telescope will be constructed.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Reaching <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> in March 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Mars_Reconnaissance_Orbiter" title="Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter">Mars Reconnaissance Orbiter</a> contained the HiRISE camera, with Primary Investigator is scientist <a href="/w/index.php?title=Alfred_McEwen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Alfred McEwen (page does not exist)">Alfred McEwen</a> as the lead on the project. This <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> mission to Mars carried a UA-designed camera expected to capture the highest-resolution images of the planet ever seen. The journey of the orbiter was 300 million miles. The project is expected to be in its Primary Science Phase in the month of October. Currently operating on the surface of <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> is the Lander known as the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_(spacecraft)" title="Phoenix (spacecraft)">Phoenix Scout Mission</a>, led by the U of A Scientist Peter Smith. The mission's purpose is to improve knowledge of the Martian Arctic. After a successful landing on Mars in May 2008, it is the first NASA mission completely controlled by a university. The <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Radio_Observatory" title="Arizona Radio Observatory">Arizona Radio Observatory</a>, a part of <a href="/wiki/Steward_Observatory" title="Steward Observatory">Steward Observatory</a>, operates the <a href="/w/index.php?title=ARO_12_m_Radio_Telescope&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ARO 12 m Radio Telescope (page does not exist)">12 Meter Telescope</a> on <a href="/wiki/Kitt_Peak" title="Kitt Peak">Kitt Peak</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_Hertz_Submillimeter_Telescope" title="Heinrich Hertz Submillimeter Telescope">Submillimeter Telescope</a> on <a href="/wiki/Mount_Graham" title="Mount Graham">Mount Graham</a>.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Science_Foundation" title="National Science Foundation">National Science Foundation</a> funded the <a href="/wiki/IPlant_Collaborative" title="IPlant Collaborative">iPlant Collaborative</a> in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2011, the University announced that it would assume full ownership of the <a href="/wiki/Biosphere_2" title="Biosphere 2">Biosphere 2</a> scientific research facility in <a href="/wiki/Oracle,_Arizona" title="Oracle, Arizona">Oracle, Arizona</a>, north of Tucson, effective July 1.<sup id="cite_ref-UANewsBiosphere_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UANewsBiosphere-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Biosphere 2 was constructed by private developers (funded mainly by Texas businessman and philanthropist <a href="/wiki/Ed_Bass" title="Ed Bass">Ed Bass</a>) with its first <a href="/wiki/Closed_ecological_system" title="Closed ecological system">closed system</a> experiment commencing in 1991. The University had been the official management partner of the facility for research purposes since 2007.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries">Libraries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Libraries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UAmainlibr_1008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/UAmainlibr_1008.jpg/220px-UAmainlibr_1008.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/UAmainlibr_1008.jpg/330px-UAmainlibr_1008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/UAmainlibr_1008.jpg/440px-UAmainlibr_1008.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UAmainlibr_1008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Entrance to the U of A main library
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2005, the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Research_Libraries" title="Association of Research Libraries">Association of Research Libraries</a>, in its &quot;Ranked Lists for Institutions for 2005&quot; (the most recent year available), ranked the UA libraries as the 33rd overall university library in North America (out of 113) based on various statistical measures of quality; this is one rank below the library of <a href="/wiki/Duke_University" title="Duke University">Duke University</a>, one rank ahead of that of <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University" title="Northwestern University">Northwestern University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> (both these schools are members, along with the UA, of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>).</p> 
     <p>As of 2009, the UA's library system contains over five million print volumes, 600,000 electronic books, and 54,000 electronic journals. The Main Library, opened in 1976, serves as the library system's reference, periodical, and administrative center; most of the main collections and special collections are housed here as well. The Main Library is located on the southeast quadrant of campus near <a href="/wiki/McKale_Center" title="McKale Center">McKale Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Stadium" title="Arizona Stadium">Arizona Stadium</a>.</p> 
     <p>In 2002, a $20 million, 100,000-square-foot (10,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) addition, the Integrated Learning Center (ILC), was completed; it is a home base for first-year students (especially those undecided on a major) which features classrooms, auditoriums, a courtyard with an alcove for vending machines, and a greatly expanded computer lab (the Information Commons) with several dozen <a href="/wiki/Gateway,_Inc." title="Gateway, Inc.">Gateway</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Macintosh" title="Apple Macintosh" class="mw-redirect">Apple Macintosh</a> G5 workstations (these computers are available for use by the general public (with some restrictions) as well as by UA students, faculty and staff). Much of the ILC was constructed underground, underneath the east end of the Mall; the ILC connects to the basement floor of the Main Library through the Information Commons. As part of the project, additional new office space for the Library was constructed on the existing fifth floor.</p> 
     <p>The Science and Engineering Library is in a nearby building from the 1960s that houses volumes and periodicals from those fields. The Music Building (on the northwest quadrant of campus where many of the fine arts disciplines are clustered) houses the Fine Arts Library, including reference collections for architecture, music (including sheet music, recordings and listening stations), and photography. There is a small library at the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Creative_Photography" title="Center for Creative Photography">Center for Creative Photography</a>, also in the fine arts complex, devoted to the art and science of photography. The Law Library is in the law building (James E. Rogers College of Law), located at the intersection of Speedway Boulevard and Mountain Avenue.</p> 
     <p>The Arizona Health Sciences Library, built in 1996, is located on the Health Sciences Center on the north end of campus and in Phoenix on the Phoenix Biomedical Campus. The library serves the Colleges of Medicine, Nursing, Pharmacy and Public Health, the University of Arizona Health Network, and is a resource for health professionals and citizens across the state.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_organizations_and_centers">Academic organizations and centers</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Academic organizations and centers">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona_Poetry_Center" title="University of Arizona Poetry Center">The University of Arizona Poetry Center</a> is among the nation’s finest and most extensive collections of contemporary poetry. It is the largest such collection that is &quot;open shelf.&quot;</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uofa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b6/Uofa.jpg/300px-Uofa.jpg" width="300" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b6/Uofa.jpg/450px-Uofa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b6/Uofa.jpg/600px-Uofa.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uofa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Student Union, Old Main, and Forbes building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The main campus sits on 380 acres (1.5&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>) in central Tucson, about one mile (1.6&nbsp;km) northeast of downtown. There are 179 buildings on the main campus. Many of the early buildings, including the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_Museum" title="Arizona State Museum">Arizona State Museum</a> buildings (one of them the 1927 main library) and Centennial Hall, were designed by <a href="/wiki/Roy_Place" title="Roy Place">Roy Place</a>, a prominent Tucson architect. It was Place's use of red brick that set the tone for the red brick facades that are a basic and ubiquitous part of nearly all UA buildings, even those built in recent decades. Indeed, almost every UA building has red brick as a major component of the design, or at the very least, a stylistic accent to harmonize it with the other buildings on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg/220px-University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg" width="220" height="100" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg/330px-University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg/440px-University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Arizona_mall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> University of Arizona Mall
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The campus is roughly divided into quadrants. The north and south sides of campus are delineated by a grassy expanse called the Mall, which stretches from Old Main eastward to the campus' eastern border at Campbell Avenue (a major north-south arterial street). The west and east sides of campus are separated roughly by Highland Avenue and the Student Union Memorial Center (see below).</p> 
     <p>The science and mathematics buildings tend to be clustered in the southwest quadrant; the intercollegiate athletics facilities to the southeast; the arts and humanities buildings to the northwest (with the dance department being a major exception as its main facilities are far to the east end of campus), with the engineering buildings in the north central area. The optical and space sciences buildings are clustered on the east side of campus near the sports stadiums and the (1976) main library.</p> 
     <p>Speedway Boulevard, one of Tucson's primary east-west arterial streets, traditionally defined the northern boundary of campus but since the 1980s, several university buildings have been constructed north of this street, expanding into a neighborhood traditionally filled with apartment complexes and single-family homes. The University has purchased a handful of these apartment complexes for student housing in recent years. Sixth Street typically defines the southern boundary, with single-family homes (many of which are rented out to students) south of this street.</p> 
     <p>Park Avenue has traditionally defined the western boundary of campus, and there is a stone wall which runs along a large portion of the east side of the street, leading to the old Main Gate, and into the driveway leading to Old Main. Along or adjacent to all of these major streets are a wide variety of retail facilities serving the student, faculty and staff population (as is the case in other similar university neighborhoods throughout the United States): shops, bookstores, bars, banks, credit unions, coffeehouses and major chain fast-food restaurants such as <a href="/wiki/Wendy%27s" title="Wendy's">Wendy's</a>, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pei_Wei_Asian_Diner" title="Pei Wei Asian Diner">Pei Wei</a>. The area near University Boulevard and Park Avenue, near the Main Gate, has been a major center of such retail activity going back to the university's early decades; many shops dating from the 1920s have been renovated since the late 1990s, other new retail shops have been built in recent years, and a nine-story <a href="/wiki/Marriott_International" title="Marriott International">Marriott</a> hotel was built in this immediate district in 1996. The Stevie Eller Dance Theater, opened in 2003 (across the Mall from <a href="/wiki/McKale_Center" title="McKale Center">McKale Center</a>) as a 28,600-square-foot (2,660&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) dedicated performance venue for the UA's dance program, one of the most highly regarded university dance departments in the United States. Designed by Gould Evans, a Phoenix-based architectural firm, the theater was awarded the 2003 Citation Award from the <a href="/wiki/American_Institute_of_Architects" title="American Institute of Architects">American Institute of Architects</a>, Arizona Chapter.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Computer_Science" title="Computer Science" class="mw-redirect">Computer Science</a> department has set up a <a href="/wiki/Webcam" title="Webcam">webcam</a> that provides a <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cs.arizona.edu/camera/">live feed</a> of the campus as seen from the top of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.arizona.edu/buildings/gould-simpson">Gould Simpson</a> building. The Berger Memorial Fountain at the west entrance of Old Main honors the UA students who lost their lives in World War I, and dates back to 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-Berger_Memorial_Fountain_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berger_Memorial_Fountain-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Arizona generates renewable energy with solar panels (photo voltaic)that have been installed on campus buildings. In 2011, the <i>Sustainable Endowments Institute</i> gave the university a College Sustainability Report Card grade of &quot;B.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainable_Endowments_Institute_Report_Card-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The oldest campus buildings are located west of Old Main. Most of the buildings east of Old Main date from the 1940s to the 1980s, with a few recent buildings constructed in the years since 1990.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Student_Union_Memorial_Center">The Student Union Memorial Center</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Student Union Memorial Center">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UAstudentu040409.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/UAstudentu040409.jpg/220px-UAstudentu040409.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/UAstudentu040409.jpg/330px-UAstudentu040409.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/UAstudentu040409.jpg/440px-UAstudentu040409.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UAstudentu040409.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Student Union Memorial Center
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The Student Union Memorial Center, located on the north side of the Mall east of Old Main, was completely reconstructed between 2000 and 2003, replacing a 270,000-square-foot (25,000&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) structure originally opened in 1951 (with additions in the 1960s). The new $60 million student union has 405,000 square feet (37,600&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>) of space on four levels, including 14 restaurants (including a <a href="/wiki/Food_court" title="Food court">food court</a> with such national chains as Burger King, <a href="/wiki/Panda_Express" title="Panda Express">Panda Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papa_John%27s_Pizza" title="Papa John's Pizza">Papa John's Pizza</a> and Chick-fil-A), a new two-level bookstore (that includes a counter for <a href="/wiki/Clinique" title="Clinique">Clinique</a> merchandise as well as an office supplies section sponsored by <a href="/wiki/Staples_Inc." title="Staples Inc.">Staples</a> with many of the same Staples-branded items found in their regular stores), 23 meeting rooms, eight lounge areas (including one dedicated to the <a href="/wiki/USS_Arizona_(BB-39)" title="USS Arizona (BB-39)">USS <i>Arizona</i></a>), a computer lab, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Postal_Service" title="United States Postal Service">U.S. Post Office</a>, a Pinkberry Frozen Yogurt, and a copy center named Fast Copy.</p> 
     <p>The building was designed to mirror the <a href="/wiki/USS_Arizona" title="USS Arizona">USS Arizona</a>. A variety of sculptures pepper the premises, decorating the air with the chimes of dog tags or the colors of refracted light in honor of those who have served. A <a href="/wiki/Bell_(instrument)" title="Bell (instrument)">bell</a> housed on the <a href="/wiki/USS_Arizona_(BB-39)" title="USS Arizona (BB-39)">USS Arizona</a>, one of the two bells rescued from the ship after the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, has a permanent home in the clock tower of the Student Union Memorial Center on campus. The bell first arrived on campus in July 1946. The bell is rung seven times on the third Wednesday of every month at 12:07&nbsp;pm – symbolic of the battleship's sinking on December 7, 1941 – to honor individuals at the UA, as well as after home football games.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S.S._Arizona_Bell_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S.S._Arizona_Bell-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="BookStores">BookStores</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: BookStores">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Arizona BookStores (UA Bookstore or UA BookStores) is a self-financed auxiliary unit within The University of Arizona Division of <a href="/wiki/Student_Affairs" title="Student Affairs" class="mw-redirect">Student Affairs</a>, meaning the BookStores operates without the aid of monies allocated from state tax, student tuition, or any other campus subsidies.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> UA BookStores serves an imperative role in the provision of financial support for student scholarships, student-led clubs and organizations (including UAs student government, ASUA), for several UA academic departments, campus media (including the campus daily paper, the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Daily_Wildcat" title="Arizona Daily Wildcat">Arizona Daily Wildcat</a>), several performance arts venues around campus, and more.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> UA BookStores operates three store locations on campus: the Main store in the Student Union Memorial Center (SUMC), the Medical store in Arizona Health Sciences Center, and the McKale Sports Stop located in the McKale Memorial Center. The organization also operates gift shops in the Flandrau Science Center, the UA Poetry Center, and the <a href="/wiki/Biosphere2" title="Biosphere2" class="mw-redirect">Biosphere2</a> located north of Tucson. Off-campus locations include remote campus stores on the UA South campus in <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Vista" title="Sierra Vista" class="mw-redirect">Sierra Vista</a> located south of <a href="/wiki/Tucson" title="Tucson" class="mw-redirect">Tucson</a>, and the new UA Downtown campus located in the historic Montgomery Ward building, designed by <a href="/wiki/Roy_Place" title="Roy Place">Roy Place</a> (during the period he also served as the official UA campus architect) in Downtown <a href="/wiki/Tucson" title="Tucson" class="mw-redirect">Tucson</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Arboretum_at_The_University_of_Arizona">The Arboretum at The University of Arizona</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The Arboretum at The University of Arizona">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Much of the main campus has been designated an <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">arboretum</a>. Plants from around the world are labeled along a self-guided plant walk. The Krutch Cactus Garden includes the tallest <a href="/wiki/Boojum_tree" title="Boojum tree" class="mw-redirect">Boojum tree</a> in the state of Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> (The university also manages <a href="/wiki/Boyce_Thompson_Arboretum_State_Park" title="Boyce Thompson Arboretum State Park">Boyce Thompson Arboretum State Park</a>, located in rural <a href="/wiki/Pinal_County,_Arizona" title="Pinal County, Arizona">Pinal County</a> about 85 miles (137&nbsp;km) north of the main campus.) Two herbaria are located on the University campus and both are referred to as &quot;ARIZ&quot; in the <i>Index Herbariorum</i></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University of Arizona, like its sister institutions <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Northern_Arizona_University" title="Northern Arizona University">Northern Arizona University</a>, is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Board_of_Regents" title="Arizona Board of Regents">Arizona Board of Regents</a> or the ABOR, a 12-member body. According to information published by the ABOR office and available on their Web site, eight volunteer members are appointed by the Governor to staggered eight-year terms; two students serve on the Board for two-year appointments, with the first year being a nonvoting apprentice year. The Governor and the Superintendent of Public Instruction serve as voting ex-officio members. The ABOR provides &quot;policy guidance&quot; and oversight to the three major degree-granting universities, as provided for by Title 15 of the <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Revised_Statutes" title="Arizona Revised Statutes">Arizona Revised Statutes</a>.</p> 
     <p>The immediate past interim president is Eugene G. Sander, who had been UA vice provost and dean of the College of Agriculture and Life Sciences; Sander began his service as president in August 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-Swedlund_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swedlund-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Ann_Weaver_Hart" title="Ann Weaver Hart">Ann Weaver Hart</a>, formerly president of <a href="/wiki/Temple_University" title="Temple University">Temple University</a>, was named the 21st president of the UA on February 17, 2012. Dr. Hart is the first female president of the UA. She began her term on July 1, 2012, replacing Eugene Sander, who retired from the University after 25 years of service as an educator and administrator.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sanderretires_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sanderretires-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The previous president, <a href="/wiki/Robert_N._Shelton" title="Robert N. Shelton">Robert N. Shelton</a>, began his tenure in 2006 and resigned in the summer of 2011 to accept the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Bowl" title="Fiesta Bowl">Fiesta Bowl</a>, (a <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">BCS</a> <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> tournament played annually in the Phoenix area).<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Shelton's predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Likins" title="Peter Likins">Peter Likins</a>, vacated his post at the conclusion of the 2005–06 academic term.<sup id="cite_ref-Swedlund_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Swedlund-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable past UA presidents include Likins, Manuel Pacheco (the first person of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> descent to lead the university and for whom the <a href="#Libraries">Integrated Learning Center</a> is named), <a href="/wiki/Homer_L._Shantz" title="Homer L. Shantz">Homer L. Shantz</a>, Henry Koffler, John Schaefer, Richard Harvill and <a href="/wiki/Rufus_B._von_KleinSmid" title="Rufus B. von KleinSmid">Rufus B. von KleinSmid</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats" title="Arizona Wildcats">Arizona Wildcats</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Like many large public universities in the U.S., sports are a major activity on campus, and receive a large operating budget. Arizona's athletic teams are nicknamed the <b>Wildcats</b>, a name derived from a 1914 football game with then California champions <a href="/wiki/Occidental_College" title="Occidental College">Occidental College</a>, where the <a href="/wiki/L.A._Times" title="L.A. Times" class="mw-redirect">L.A. Times</a> asserted that, &quot;the Arizona men showed the fight of wildcats.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-History_8_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_8-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Arizona participates in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s Division I-A in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>, which it joined in 1978.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Men's basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats_men%27s_basketball" title="Arizona Wildcats men's basketball">Arizona Wildcats men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">men's basketball</a> team has been one of the nation's most successful programs since <a href="/wiki/Lute_Olson" title="Lute Olson">Lute Olson</a> was hired as head coach in 1983, and is still known as a national powerhouse in Division I men's basketball.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Between 1985 and 2009, the team reached the NCAA Tournament 25 consecutive years, which is the second-longest streak in <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> history, 2nd only to <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels_men%27s_basketball" title="North Carolina Tar Heels men's basketball">North Carolina's</a> record of 27 consecutive appearances from 1975 to 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The Wildcats have reached the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship#Final_Four" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">Final Four</a> of the NCAA tournament in <a href="/wiki/1988_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1988 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1988</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1994 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/1997_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1997 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1997</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2001_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="2001 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">2001</a>. In 1997, Arizona defeated the <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats" title="Kentucky Wildcats">University of Kentucky</a>, the defending national champions, to win the NCAA National Championship (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Championship</a>) by a score of 84–79 in overtime; Arizona's first national championship victory. The 1997 championship team became the first and only in <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> history to defeat three number-one seeds en route to a national title (Kansas, North Carolina and Kentucky—the North Carolina game being the final game for longtime UNC head coach Dean Smith). Point guard <a href="/wiki/Miles_Simon" title="Miles Simon">Miles Simon</a> was chosen as 1997 <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Basketball_Tournament_Most_Outstanding_Player" title="NCAA Basketball Tournament Most Outstanding Player">Final Four MVP</a> (Simon was also an assistant coach under Olson from 2005 to 2008). The Cats also boast the third highest winning percentage in the nation over the last twenty years. Arizona has won a total of 21 conference championships in its programs history. Since the institution of the two-round draft system in 1989 by the NBA, no school has had more draft picks than Arizona.<sup id="cite_ref-Draft_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Draft-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Wildcats play their home games at the <a href="/wiki/McKale_Center" title="McKale Center">McKale Center</a> in Tucson. A number of former Wildcats have gone on to pursue successful professional NBA careers (especially during the Lute Olson era), including <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Arenas" title="Gilbert Arenas">Gilbert Arenas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Jefferson" title="Richard Jefferson">Richard Jefferson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Bibby" title="Mike Bibby">Mike Bibby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jason_Terry" title="Jason Terry">Jason Terry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sean_Elliott" title="Sean Elliott">Sean Elliott</a>, <a href="/wiki/Damon_Stoudamire" title="Damon Stoudamire">Damon Stoudamire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Reeves" title="Khalid Reeves">Khalid Reeves</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luke_Walton" title="Luke Walton">Luke Walton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hassan_Adams" title="Hassan Adams">Hassan Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salim_Stoudamire" title="Salim Stoudamire">Salim Stoudamire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Iguodala" title="Andre Iguodala">Andre Iguodala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Channing_Frye" title="Channing Frye">Channing Frye</a>, Brian Williams (later known as <a href="/wiki/Bison_Dele" title="Bison Dele">Bison Dele</a>), Sean Rooks, Jud Buechler, Michael Dickerson, <a href="/wiki/Chase_Budinger" title="Chase Budinger">Chase Budinger</a>, Jordan Hill, Jerryd Bayless, Derrick Williams and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Kerr" title="Steve Kerr">Steve Kerr</a>. <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Lofton" title="Kenny Lofton">Kenny Lofton</a>, now best known as a former Major League Baseball star, was a four-year letter winner as a Wildcat basketball player (and was on the 1988 Final Four team), before one year on the Arizona baseball team. Another notable former Wildcat basketball player is <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Edgerson" title="Eugene Edgerson">Eugene Edgerson</a>, who played on the 1997 and 2001 Final Four squads, and is currently one of the primary stars of the <a href="/wiki/Harlem_Globetrotters" title="Harlem Globetrotters">Harlem Globetrotters</a> as &quot;Wildkat&quot; Edgerson.</p> 
     <p>Before Lute Olson's hire in 1983, Arizona was the first major Division I school to hire an African American head coach in <a href="/wiki/Fred_Snowden" title="Fred Snowden">Fred Snowden</a>, in 1972. After a 25-year tenure as Arizona head coach, Olson announced his retirement from the Arizona basketball program in October 2008. After two seasons of using interim coaches, Arizona named <a href="/wiki/Sean_Miller" title="Sean Miller">Sean Miller</a>, head coach at <a href="/wiki/Xavier_University" title="Xavier University">Xavier University</a>, as its new head basketball coach in April 2009.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats_football" title="Arizona Wildcats football">Arizona Wildcats football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg/220px-Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg/330px-Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg/440px-Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Arizona_Football_-_Nick_Foles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Nick Foles, a quarterback for Arizona passes the ball against UCLA.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Football" title="American Football" class="mw-redirect">football</a> team began at The University of Arizona in 1899 under the nickname &quot;Varsity&quot; (a name kept until the 1914 season when the team was deemed the &quot;Wildcats&quot;).<sup id="cite_ref-History_7_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_7-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The football team was notably successful in the 1990s, under head coach <a href="/wiki/Dick_Tomey" title="Dick Tomey">Dick Tomey</a>; his &quot;Desert Swarm&quot; defense was characterized by tough, hard-nosed tactics. In 1993, the team had its first 10-win season and beat the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Hurricanes_football" title="Miami Hurricanes football">University of Miami</a> Hurricanes in the <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Bowl" title="Fiesta Bowl">Fiesta Bowl</a> by a score of 29–0. It was the bowl game's only shutout in its then 23-year history. In 1998, the team posted a school-record 12–1 season and made the <a href="/wiki/Holiday_Bowl" title="Holiday Bowl">Holiday Bowl</a> in which it defeated the <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Cornhuskers_football" title="Nebraska Cornhuskers football">Nebraska Cornhuskers</a>. Arizona ended that season ranked 4th nationally in the coaches and API poll. The 1998 Holiday Bowl was televised on <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a> and set the now-surpassed record of being the most watched of any bowl game in that network's history (the current record belongs to the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Alamo_Bowl" title="Alamo Bowl">Alamo Bowl</a> between <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Wolverines_football" title="Michigan Wolverines football">Michigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Nebraska" title="University of Nebraska" class="mw-redirect">Nebraska</a>). From November 2003 until October 2011, the program was led by <a href="/wiki/Mike_Stoops" title="Mike Stoops">Mike Stoops</a>, brother of <a href="/wiki/Bob_Stoops" title="Bob Stoops">Bob Stoops</a>, the head football coach at the <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Sooners_football" title="Oklahoma Sooners football">University of Oklahoma</a> (the 2000 <a href="/wiki/BCS_National_Championship" title="BCS National Championship" class="mw-redirect">BCS national champions</a>); Stoops was fired on October 10, 2011. Former Michigan and <a href="/wiki/West_Virginia_Mountaineers_football" title="West Virginia Mountaineers football">West Virginia</a> head coach <a href="/wiki/Rich_Rodriguez" title="Rich Rodriguez">Rich Rodriguez</a> was hired on November 21, 2011 to lead the Wildcats. The announcement was made by UA athletic director <a href="/wiki/Gregory_Byrne" title="Gregory Byrne">Greg Byrne</a> via Twitter. In his first season, Rich Rodriguez took the Arizona Wildcats to the <a href="/wiki/2012_New_Mexico_Bowl" title="2012 New Mexico Bowl">2012 New Mexico Bowl</a>, where they defeated the Nevada Wolfpack.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baseball">Baseball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Baseball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats_baseball" title="Arizona Wildcats baseball">Arizona Wildcats baseball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The baseball team had its first season in 1904. The baseball team has captured four national championship titles in 1976, 1980, 1986 and 2012, with the first three coached by <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Kindall" title="Jerry Kindall">Jerry Kindall</a> and the most recent by <a href="/wiki/Andy_Lopez" title="Andy Lopez">Andy Lopez</a>. Arizona baseball teams have appeared in the NCAA National Championship title series a total of eight times, including 1956, 1959, 1963, 1976, 1980, 1986, 2004 and 2012 (<a href="/wiki/College_World_Series" title="College World Series">College World Series</a>). Arizona has appeared in 34 baseball tournaments in its rich history. Arizona is 7th all-time in games won in the regular season with 2,347 wins. Home games are played at <a href="/wiki/Hi_Corbett_Field" title="Hi Corbett Field">Hi Corbett Field</a>.</p> 
     <p>The team is currently coached by <a href="/wiki/Andy_Lopez" title="Andy Lopez">Andy Lopez</a>; aided by Assistant Coach <a href="/w/index.php?title=Matt_Siegal&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Matt Siegal (page does not exist)">Matt Siegal</a>, Assistant Coach <a href="/w/index.php?title=Shaun_Cole&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Shaun Cole (page does not exist)">Shaun Cole</a> and Volunteer Assistant Coach <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brett_Scyphers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brett Scyphers (page does not exist)">Brett Scyphers</a>. Arizona baseball also has a student section named The Hot Corner. Famous UA baseball alums include <a href="/wiki/Terry_Francona" title="Terry Francona">Terry Francona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Lofton" title="Kenny Lofton">Kenny Lofton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shelley_Duncan" title="Shelley Duncan">Shelley Duncan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Trevor_Hoffman" title="Trevor Hoffman">Trevor Hoffman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Melancon" title="Mark Melancon">Mark Melancon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chip_Hale" title="Chip Hale">Chip Hale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Craig_Lefferts" title="Craig Lefferts">Craig Lefferts</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._T._Snow" title="J. T. Snow">J. T. Snow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Lee_(baseball)" title="Don Lee (baseball)">Don Lee</a>, Carl Thomas, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Paul" title="Mike Paul">Mike Paul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dan_Schneider_(baseball)" title="Dan Schneider (baseball)">Dan Schneider</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rich_Hinton" title="Rich Hinton">Rich Hinton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Vosberg" title="Ed Vosberg">Ed Vosberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Leiber" title="Hank Leiber">Hank Leiber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ron_Hassey" title="Ron Hassey">Ron Hassey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brad_Mills_(infielder)" title="Brad Mills (infielder)" class="mw-redirect">Brad Mills</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joe_Magrane" title="Joe Magrane">Joe Magrane</a>, and Tyler Cook.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Softball">Softball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Softball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Wildcats_softball" title="Arizona Wildcats softball">Arizona Wildcats softball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The Arizona <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> team is among the top programs in the country. The softball team has won eight <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> Women's College World Series titles, in 1991, 1993, 1994, 1996, 1997, 2001, 2006 and 2007 under head coach <a href="/wiki/Mike_Candrea" title="Mike Candrea">Mike Candrea</a> (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Softball_Championship" title="NCAA Softball Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Softball Championship</a>). The team has appeared in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> National Championship in 1991, 1992, 1993, 1994, 1995, 1996, 1997 1998, 2001, 2002, 2006, 2007 and 2010 (a feat second only to <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a>), and has reached the College World Series 19 of the past 20 years. Coach Candrea, along with former Arizona pitcher <a href="/wiki/Jennie_Finch" title="Jennie Finch">Jennie Finch</a>, led the 2004 U.S. Olympic softball team to a gold medal in <a href="/wiki/Athens,_Greece" title="Athens, Greece" class="mw-redirect">Athens, Greece</a>. The Wildcat softball team plays at <a href="/wiki/Rita_Hillenbrand_Memorial_Stadium" title="Rita Hillenbrand Memorial Stadium">Rita Hillenbrand Memorial Stadium</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_and_women.27s_golf">Men's and women's golf</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Men's and women's golf">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university's golf teams have also been notably successful. The men's team won a national championship in 1992 (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_Men%27s_Golf_Championships" title="NCAA Division I Men's Golf Championships">NCAA Division I Men's Golf Championships</a>), and has produced a number of successful professionals, most notably <a href="/wiki/Jim_Furyk" title="Jim Furyk">Jim Furyk</a>. The women's team won national championships in 1996 and 2000 (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Golf_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Golf Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Women's Golf Championship</a>). Few if any women's golf programs can boast two more illustrious alumni than the Wildcats' two greatest products—<a href="/wiki/Annika_S%C3%B6renstam" title="Annika S&ouml;renstam">Annika S&ouml;renstam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lorena_Ochoa" title="Lorena Ochoa">Lorena Ochoa</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_lacrosse">Men's lacrosse</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Men's lacrosse">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The lacrosse team is a club team, not a varsity sport at Arizona, affectionately known as the “Laxcats”. Its existence, since the mid-1960s, is saturated with a rich tradition of success. In the 60’s, Arizona was a Division I Varsity program, coached by the legendary <a href="/wiki/Carl_Runk" title="Carl Runk">Carl Runk</a>, an Arizona graduate and football player. In 1998 Carl retired after twenty-eight years at <a href="/wiki/Towson_University" title="Towson University">Towson University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Maryland" title="Maryland">Maryland</a>.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Many other Wildcats have met with success at the University. Alix Creek and Michelle Oldham won the NCAA Women's Doubles Tennis title in 1993, defeating Texas in the Final. Although surprising to some, the University of Arizona has a noteworthy history in <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. The school's club hockey team, known as the Icecats, has won over 600 games since its inception in 1978. The Icecats defeated <a href="/wiki/Penn_State" title="Penn State" class="mw-redirect">Penn State</a> for the National Collegiate Club Hockey National Championship in 1985. They are now part of <a href="/wiki/ACHA" title="ACHA" class="mw-redirect">ACHA</a> Division I. Robert M. Tanita was a nationally ranked collegiate wrestler who reached the NCAA finals tournament as WAC champion in 1963.</p> 
     <p>Three national championships for <a href="/wiki/Synchronized_swimming" title="Synchronized swimming">synchronized swimming</a> were won in 1980, 1981, and 1984, though these championships were in the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association of Intercollegiate Athletics for Women" class="mw-redirect">Association of Intercollegiate Athletics for Women</a>, and not the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>. Along with winning three national championships in the pool for synchronized swimming, the Wildcats have also won their first <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> Championship in men and women’s <a href="/w/index.php?title=Swimming_and_diving&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Swimming and diving (page does not exist)">swimming and diving</a> for the seasons of 2007–2008. Topping off these weekends <a href="/wiki/Frank_Busch" title="Frank Busch">Frank Busch</a>, the men and women’s head coach, was named <a href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA" class="mw-redirect">NCAA</a> Swimming Coach of the Year. Arizona men became the first team to claim a first-time title since UCLA’s win in 1982. Also, the men ended Texas and Auburn’s winning streak since 1998. At the end of the meet, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas" title="University of Texas" class="mw-redirect">University of Texas</a> took second while 2007’s champion, <a href="/wiki/Auburn_University" title="Auburn University">Auburn University</a>, took fifth. For the women, Arizona worked on the disappointment of 2007’s defeat. The women were winning until the last day when Auburn grasped the title. Unlike 2007, Arizona’s women did not let anyone come close. The Wildcats won with 484 team points while <a href="/wiki/Auburn_University" title="Auburn University">Auburn University</a> came in second with 348 and <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> in third with 343. Student-athletes from the women's swimming and diving team have been particularly heralded by the NCAA. The <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Woman_of_the_Year_Award" title="NCAA Woman of the Year Award">NCAA Woman of the Year Award</a> was won by UA swimmers Whitney Myers, Lacey Nymeyer and Justine Schluntz in 2007, 2009 and 2010 respectively. The three awards and the 1994 award won by track and field athlete Tanya Hughes are the highest number of Woman of the Year awards won by a single university.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Individual_national_championships">Individual national championships</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Individual national championships">edit</a>]</span></h3>
