     <p>A number of notable individuals have also won national championships in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>. These include <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Beard" title="Amanda Beard">Amanda Beard</a> in 2001 for swimming and <a href="/wiki/Annika_S%C3%B6renstam" title="Annika S&ouml;renstam">Annika S&ouml;renstam</a> in 1991 in golf. The men's <a href="/wiki/Cross_country_running" title="Cross country running">cross country</a> has also produced two individual national titles in 1986 (Aaron Ramirez) and 1994 (Martin Keino) (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Cross_Country_Championship" title="NCAA Men's Cross Country Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Men's Cross Country Champions</a>). The women's cross country also produced two individual national titles in 1996 (Amy Skieresz) and 2001 (Tara Chaplin) (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Cross_Country_Championship" title="NCAA Women's Cross Country Championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA Women's Cross Country Championship</a>). Another notable individual was football standout <a href="/wiki/Vance_Johnson" title="Vance Johnson">Vance Johnson</a> who won the NCAA long jump in 1982. Arizona's first NCAA Individual Champion in the sport of Men's Swimming came in 1981 when Doug Towne won the 500 yard freestyle at the NCAA championships. Another individual champion occurred in 1989 when Mariusz Podkoscielny swimming won the 1650-yard (mile) at the NCAA National Championships held at the IUPUI Natatorium.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>A strong athletic rivalry exists between the University of Arizona and <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Tempe,_Arizona" title="Tempe, Arizona">Tempe</a>. The UA leads the all-time record against ASU in men's basketball (145–80), football (47–38–1), and baseball (234–202–1). The football rivalry game between the schools is known as &quot;The Duel in the Desert.&quot; The trophy awarded after each game, the <a href="/wiki/Territorial_Cup" title="Territorial Cup">Territorial Cup</a>, is the nation's oldest rivalry trophy, distinguished by the NCAA. Rivalries have also been created with other <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pac-12</a> teams, especially <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Los_Angeles" title="University of California, Los Angeles">University of California, Los Angeles</a> which has provided a worthy <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> rival and was Arizona's main basketball rival in the early and mid-1990s.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University's mascots are a pair of <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphized" title="Anthropomorphized" class="mw-redirect">anthropomorphized</a> <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">wildcats</a> named <a href="/wiki/Wilbur_and_Wilma" title="Wilbur and Wilma">Wilbur and Wilma</a>. The identities of Wilbur and Wilma are kept secret through the year as the mascots appear only in costume. In 1986, Wilbur married his longtime wildcat girlfriend, Wilma. Together, Wilbur and Wilma appear along with the <a href="/wiki/Cheerleading" title="Cheerleading">cheerleading</a> squad at most Wildcat sporting events.<sup id="cite_ref-Wilber_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wilber-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Arizona's first mascot was a real desert <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">bobcat</a> named &quot;Rufus Arizona&quot;, introduced in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-History_10_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_10-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Wilbur was originally created by Bob White as a cartoon character in the University's humor magazine, <i>Kitty Kat</i>. From 1915 through the 1950s the school mascot was a live <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">bobcat</a>, a species known locally as a wildcat. This succession of live mascots were known by the common name of Rufus Arizona, originally named after Rufus von Kleinsmid, president of the university from 1914 to 1921. 1959 marked the creation of the first incarnated Wilbur, when University student John Paquette and his roommate, Dick Heller, came up with idea of creating a costume for a student to wear. Ed Stuckenhoff was chosen to wear the costume at the homecoming game in 1959 against Texas Tech and since then it has become a long-standing tradition. Wilbur celebrated his 50th birthday in November 2009.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song">Fight song</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fight song">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 1952 Jack K. Lee, an applicant for the UA's band directorship, departed Tucson by air following an interview with UA administration. From his airplane window, Lee observed the huge letters on the roof of the UA gymnasium reading &quot;BEAR DOWN.&quot; Inspired, Lee scribbled down the music and lyrics to an up-tempo song. By the time his plane landed, he had virtually finished it. A few weeks later Lee was named the UA band director, and in September 1952, the UA band performed &quot;Bear Down, Arizona!&quot; in public for the first time. Soon thereafter, &quot;Bear Down, Arizona!&quot; became accepted as UA's fight song (<a href="/wiki/Bear_Down" title="Bear Down">Bear Down</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Berger_Memorial_Fountain_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berger_Memorial_Fountain-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="ZonaZoo">ZonaZoo</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: ZonaZoo">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Officially implemented in 2003, ZonaZoo is the official student section and student ticketing program for the University of Arizona Athletics. The ZonaZoo program is co-owned by the Associated Students of the University of Arizona (ASUA) and Arizona Athletics yet run by a team of individuals called the ZonaZoo Crew. ZonaZoo is one of the largest and most spirited in NCAA Division I Athletics and the largest in the PAC12.<br style="clear:both;" /></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_venues">Notable venues</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Notable venues">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/McKale_Center" title="McKale Center">McKale Center</a>, which opened in 1973, is currently used by men's and women's basketball, women's gymnastics, and women's volleyball. The official capacity has changed often. The largest crowd to see a game in McKale was 15,176 in 1976 for a game against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Mexico" title="University of New Mexico">University of New Mexico</a>, a main rival during that period. In 2000, the floor in McKale was dubbed Lute Olson Court, for the basketball program's winningest coach. During a memorial service in 2001 for Lute's wife, Bobbi, who died after a battle with ovarian cancer, the floor was renamed Lute and Bobbi Olson Court. In addition to the playing surface, McKale Center is host to the offices of the UA athletic department. McKale Center is named after J.F. Pop McKale, who was athletic director and coach from 1914 through 1957. Joe Cavaleri (&quot;The Ooh-Aah Man&quot;) made his dramatic and inspiring appearances there. <a href="/wiki/Arizona_Stadium" title="Arizona Stadium">Arizona Stadium</a>, built in 1928 and last expanded in 1976, seats over 56,000 patrons. It hosts <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> games and has also been used for university graduations. The turf is <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_grass" title="Bermuda grass" class="mw-redirect">bermuda grass</a>, taken from the local Tucson National Golf Club. Arizona football's home record is 258–139–12. The largest crowd ever in Arizona Stadium was 59,920 in 1996 for a game against Arizona State University. <a href="/wiki/Rita_Hillenbrand_Memorial_Stadium" title="Rita Hillenbrand Memorial Stadium">Rita Hillenbrand Memorial Stadium</a> hosts <a href="/wiki/Softball" title="Softball">softball</a> games. <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Kindall_Field_at_Frank_Sancet_Stadium" title="Jerry Kindall Field at Frank Sancet Stadium">Jerry Kindall Field at Frank Sancet Stadium</a> hosted baseball games until the 2012 season, when the baseball program began playing home games at <a href="/wiki/Hi_Corbett_Field" title="Hi Corbett Field">Hi Corbett Field</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Cactus_League" title="Cactus League" class="mw-redirect">Cactus League</a> <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> facility located three miles southeast of campus.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognized_fraternities_and_sororities_of_the_Greek_System">Recognized fraternities and sororities of the Greek System</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Recognized fraternities and sororities of the Greek System">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>There are currently (2005) 44 <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities" title="Fraternities and sororities" class="mw-redirect">fraternity and sorority</a> chapters that are recognized by the University of Arizona. As of 2006, approximately 10.3% of male UA students were members of campus fraternities, and 10.8% of female students were members of sororities. The fraternities and sororities are governed by 4 governing councils. The <i>Interfraternity Council (IFC)</i> represents 25 fraternities, the <i>National Pan-Hellenic Council (NPHC)</i> represents 6 historically African-American fraternities and sororities, the <i>Panhellenic Association (PHC)</i> represents 20 sororities and the <i>United Sorority and Fraternity Council (USFC)</i> represents 10 multicultural and multi-interest Greek organizations.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Delta Chi Lambda is an Asian American sorority that was established at the University of Arizona in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Lambda chapter of <a href="/wiki/Phrateres" title="Phrateres">Phrateres</a>, a non-exclusive, non-profit social-service club, was installed here in 1937. Between 1924 and 1967, 23 chapters of Phrateres were installed in universities across North America. There is a Facebook group for all alumni of the Lambda chapter.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognized_student_clubs_and_organizations">Recognized student clubs and organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Recognized student clubs and organizations">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>As mentioned earlier, a new and expansive Student Union building,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> opened in 2003; it is the largest student union in the U.S. not affiliated with a hotel. The University of Arizona is home to more than 500 philanthropic, multi-cultural, social, athletic, academic, and student clubs and campus organizations. A listing is found at Associated Students of The University of Arizona (ASUA)<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> through the Student Union. CSIL also houses the Arizona Blue Chip Program<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> one of the largest collegiate-level leadership development programs in the United States, with over 500 active students at any one time throughout the 4 years of the program. Blue Chip was founded in 1999 and has formed a partnership with the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wollongong" title="University of Wollongong">University of Wollongong</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Wollongong,_New_South_Wales" title="Wollongong, New South Wales" class="mw-redirect">Wollongong</a>, Australia where a sister program, the Black Opal Leadership Development Program<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> began in February 2005. Structure, curriculum, students and even staff are exchanged between the two institutions in a unique international leadership development initiative. Also located in the CSIL is the office of <a href="/wiki/Camp_Wildcat" title="Camp Wildcat" class="mw-redirect">Camp Wildcat</a>, a student-run non-profit service organization that serves local disadvantaged youth. Through funding from the CSIL and the Associated Students of the University of Arizona, clubs are given the resources and encouragement to explore unusual interests.</p> 
     <p>In 2008 University of Arizona students started <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://clubs.asua.arizona.edu/~asfl_ua/">their own branch</a> (reinstated as of April 21, 2010<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup>) of the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.arizonastudentsforlife.org/">Arizona Students for Life (ASFL)</a> <a href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life">pro-life</a> association, whose goal is to help pregnant college women and raise awareness about <a href="/wiki/Abortion" title="Abortion">elective abortion</a>, of which college women are half all those affected.</p> 
     <p>The University of Arizona is also home to one of the oldest <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://arizonamun.org">Model United Nations</a> organizations in the United States, which each year hosts several hundred students high school students in a bilingual simulation of the United Nations and other international bodies.</p> 
     <p>Officially recognized in February 2012, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sseosyndicate.com">U of A SEO Club</a> is dedicated to creating the foundation for developing <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_optimization" title="Search engine optimization">search engine optimization</a> curriculum and integrating it into several campus departments.</p> 
     <p>In 2008, the Office of Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual, Transgender, and Questioning Student Affairs was created to provide services to <a href="/wiki/LGBTQ" title="LGBTQ" class="mw-redirect">LGBTQ</a> students and staff on campus<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> and serve opposite an existing student group called “Pride Alliance,”<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> a recognized LGBTQ student group that has been active since the 1990s in providing support and visibility to LGBTQ students on campus.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Performance_groups">Performance groups</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Performance groups">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The campus comedy group, <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Corner" title="Comedy Corner">Comedy Corner</a> is a sketch and improv comedy group at the University of Arizona. Started in 1979 by Adam Goldstein, it claims to be the nation's oldest weekly college sketch and improv comedy group, though in recent years it has branched out into doing previously videotaped comedy bits and shorts as well. Comedy Corner was the first documented college sketch comedy troupe to incorporate improvisation into its weekly shows, a practice that has become more common in recent years.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditions">Traditions</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Traditions">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>At the beginning of each school year, freshmen repaint the &quot;A&quot; on <a href="/wiki/Sentinel_Peak_(Arizona)" title="Sentinel Peak (Arizona)">&quot;A&quot; Mountain</a>, and since 1914 the &quot;A&quot; remains a <a href="/wiki/Tucson" title="Tucson" class="mw-redirect">Tucson</a> and Wildcat landmark.<sup id="cite_ref-History_9_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_9-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The &quot;A&quot; is now painted Red, White and Blue until all troops in foreign wars steming from the September 11 attacks return home. This was passed by the ASUA student government body shortly after the war in Afghanistan began in 2001. Later in the school year, Spring Fling, an ASUA Student Government program, and the largest student-run carnival in the U.S., has been held annually by UA students since 1965, under a different name: The Rites of Spring. The event occurs every April, and brings together the U of A community and the Tucson community. The UA club, <a href="/wiki/Camp_Wildcat" title="Camp Wildcat" class="mw-redirect">Camp Wildcat</a>, initially began the festival as a fundraiser and continued to do so until the event was taken over by <a href="/w/index.php?title=ASUA&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ASUA (page does not exist)">ASUA</a> in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-Spring_Fling_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spring_Fling-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marching_band">Marching band</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Marching band">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Arizona <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a>, named <a href="/wiki/The_Pride_of_Arizona" title="The Pride of Arizona">The Pride of Arizona</a>, played at the halftime of the first <a href="/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a>. Most recently, the Pride was named one of the top five marching bands in the nation. They are directed by Professor Jay C. Rees. Instrumentation includes woodwinds, brass, and a marching percussion section, as well as a pomline, twirling line, and color guard.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="School_colors">School colors</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: School colors">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The current school colors are UA Red and UA Blue, recognized in the <a href="/wiki/Pantone_Matching_System" title="Pantone Matching System" class="mw-redirect">Pantone Matching System</a>, with the PMS number 200 and 281, respectively. In CMYK system, process color for the UA Red is C: 0 M:100 Y:65 K:15, and C:100 M:72 Y:0 K:38 for the UA Blue. Before 1900, the colors were sage green and silver. The switch was made when a lucrative discount on red and blue jerseys became available.<sup id="cite_ref-Colors_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colors-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_government_representation">Student government representation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student government representation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>Overall, students at the University of Arizona have been represented by the Associated Students of the University of Arizona (ASUA) since 1913. Every year (usually in March), the students elect 10 Senators At-Large, an Administrative Vice President, an Executive Vice President and President to 1-year terms. The ASUA oversees the ZonaZoo and UA Spring Fling programs, while holding administrative oversight for the nearly 500 student clubs on campus. The organization appoints 4 Directors to serve on the student funded and led Arizona Students' Association. Each of the 10 Senators and all Administrative Officers also are appointed to serve on the various University of Arizona Faculty and Administrative Committees.</p> 
     <p>In 1997, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Graduate_and_Professional_Student_Council&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Graduate and Professional Student Council (page does not exist)">Graduate and Professional Student Council</a> (GPSC) split from the ASUA and has since become the <i>de facto</i> body to represent issues specific to graduate and professional students. Each year (usually in late March or early April), the graduate and professional students elect 30 representatives by constituency in accordance to College graduate and/or professional student population, with three of those representatives elected at large. The Vice President and President are also elected at large by the graduate and professional student body. Much like ASUA, the GPSC appoints representatives to serve on various University of Arizona Faculty and Administrative Committees and 1 Director to serve on the Arizona Students' Association.</p> 
     <p>On-Campus residents also have their own Student Leadership Organization known as the &quot;Residence Hall Association&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> Anyone who lives on campus is automatically a member of RHA. The individual subunits of RHA consist of the hall councils of all <a href="/w/index.php?title=22_residence_halls&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="22 residence halls (page does not exist)">22 residence halls</a>. Each Hall Council is one of three structures, Traditional, Hybrid and Open. Additionally each hall council has a EcoRep for Sustainability, and two RHA Representatives who are sent to represent their hall at RHA General Body Meetings and one ACT Rep for Diversity. At these meetings, the gathered representatives and RHA Executive Board, elected from within the RHA General Body, discuss issues and make decisions concerning all 6,000 on campus residents. Members of the RHA Executive Board are elected to one-year terms during February and March and are sworn into office at the RHA Banquet usually held during the later part of April. Hall council members and RHA representatives are usually elected by the residents of their respective residence halls during the first 2 weeks of the Fall semester in late August and early September with their term running through the end of the Spring semester in early May. The RHA Executive Board consists of 7 different elected positions (President, Vice President of Public Relations, National Communications Coordinator, Vice President of Finances, Vice President of Operations, Vice President of Services, and Vice President of Programming) along with an appointed Parliamentarian position and an advisor known as the Coordinator for Student Leadership. In 2011, the Residence Hall Association revamped its Executive Board in effort to make the EBoard more parallel to the IACURH Regional Board and NACURH National Board. The Vice President of Finances and Vice President of Operations positions were merged to form the &quot;Vice President of Business Administration&quot; while a new position formed known as the &quot;Vice President of Training and Development&quot;.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Arizona Residence Hall Association has hosted 3 regional IACURH Residence Hall Conferences, which were hosted in 1961, 1997, and 2004 and a &quot;No Frills&quot; Business meeting in 2013<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup>. In 2005 and 2012 the University of Arizona's Residence Hall Association was voted by <a href="/wiki/NACURH" title="NACURH" class="mw-redirect">NACURH</a> (National Association of College and University Residence Halls) as the National School of the Year out of over 400 schools across the United States. In May 2009, the University of Arizona hosted the NACURH National Residence Hall Conference (also hosted in 1963), bringing more than 2,200 on-campus residents from over 250 schools across the United States and Canada for 3 days of school spirit and learning how to become more sustainable and socially just. The conference theme (Our Place in Time) focused on sustainability and social justice within the residence halls.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Arizona_in_film_and_literature">Arizona in film and literature</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Arizona in film and literature">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The University has made itself known through many films and television appearances. The film <i><a href="/wiki/Revenge_of_the_Nerds" title="Revenge of the Nerds">Revenge of the Nerds</a></i> (1984) was filmed at the University of Arizona. In the movie, the Alpha Beta &quot;jock&quot; house was the real-life home to the UA chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Rho" title="Alpha Gamma Rho">Alpha Gamma Rho</a> Fraternity until purchased by the <a href="/wiki/Beta_Theta_Pi" title="Beta Theta Pi">Beta Theta Pi</a> fraternity in 2006. The dorm room (with the balcony) seen in the film is located on the third floor of historic <a href="/wiki/Cochise_Hall" title="Cochise Hall">Cochise Hall</a> on campus. When the characters are moving in at the beginning of the movie, the dorm behind the post office drop is Yuma Hall.</p> 
     <p>In the 1994 film <i><a href="/wiki/Speed_(1994_film)" title="Speed (1994 film)">Speed</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Hopper" title="Dennis Hopper">Dennis Hopper</a> refers to <a href="/wiki/Sandra_Bullock" title="Sandra Bullock">Sandra Bullock</a>'s character as a Wildcat because of the emblem on her sweater.</p> 
     <p>In the 1989 film &quot;<a href="/wiki/Leviathan" title="Leviathan">Leviathan</a>&quot;, <a href="/wiki/Peter_Weller" title="Peter Weller">Peter Weller</a>'s character, Steven Beck, frequently wears an Arizona Wildcats hat. In the 2006 film <i><a href="/wiki/You,_Me_and_Dupree" title="You, Me and Dupree">You, Me and Dupree</a></i>, produced by Arizona Alum Scott Stuber, several characters are watching the Arizona Wildcats play football against <a href="/wiki/Washington_State_University" title="Washington State University">Washington State University</a>. While playing in their blue uniforms, Arizona scores on a fumble recovery.</p> 
     <p>The film <i><a href="/wiki/Eating_Out" title="Eating Out">Eating Out</a></i> was shot around the University of Arizona campus in Tucson.</p> 
     <p>An episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Little_House_on_the_Prairie_(TV_series)" title="Little House on the Prairie (TV series)">Little House on the Prairie</a></i>, entitled &quot;A Wiser Heart,&quot; used Old Main as a prominent backdrop throughout.</p> 
     <p>The film <i><a href="/wiki/Night_of_the_Lepus" title="Night of the Lepus">Night of the Lepus</a></i> (1972) features a short shot of <a href="/wiki/Old_Main" title="Old Main" class="mw-redirect">Old Main</a> in the first few minutes. The University appears at the end of the film as well.</p> 
     <p>The University has also been the setting for portions of <a href="/wiki/David_Foster_Wallace" title="David Foster Wallace">David Foster Wallace</a>'s novel <i><a href="/wiki/Infinite_Jest" title="Infinite Jest">Infinite Jest</a></i> takes place at the University of Arizona campus, including a scene in the administration building satirizing the school's <a href="/wiki/Bureaucracy" title="Bureaucracy">bureaucracy</a>. Wallace was an alumnus of UA.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_staff">Notable alumni and staff</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Arizona&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and staff">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Arizona_people" title="List of University of Arizona people">List of University of Arizona people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Notable alumni include U.S. Representative (Arizona's 7th congressional district) <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_M._Grijalva" title="Ra&uacute;l M. Grijalva" class="mw-redirect">Ra&uacute;l M. Grijalva</a>; the creator of the television series <i><a href="/wiki/Sesame_Street" title="Sesame Street">Sesame Street</a></i> and founder of the Children's Television Workshop <a href="/wiki/Joan_Ganz_Cooney" title="Joan Ganz Cooney">Joan Ganz Cooney</a>; pop singer <a href="/wiki/Linda_Ronstadt" title="Linda Ronstadt">Linda Ronstadt</a>; <a href="/wiki/Brian_Schmidt" title="Brian Schmidt">Brian Schmidt</a>, winner of 2011 Nobel Prize in Physics (1989); <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Kingsolver" title="Barbara Kingsolver">Barbara Kingsolver</a>, author awarded the National Humanities Medal in 2000; Actor and television personality <a href="/wiki/Greg_Kinnear" title="Greg Kinnear">Greg Kinnear</a>; former Mayor of <a href="/wiki/Palm_Springs,_California" title="Palm Springs, California">Palm Springs, California</a> (1995––2003) <a href="/w/index.php?title=William_G._Kleindienst&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="William G. Kleindienst (page does not exist)">William G. Kleindienst</a>; and several <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> astronauts. Two <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="Nobel Prize laureates by university affiliation" class="mw-redirect">Nobel laureate</a> on the faculty are members of the College of Optical Sciences: <a href="/wiki/Nicolaas_Bloembergen" title="Nicolaas Bloembergen">Nicolaas Bloembergen</a> (Physics, 1981) and <a href="/wiki/Willis_E._Lamb" title="Willis E. Lamb" class="mw-redirect">Willis E. Lamb</a> (Physics, 1955). The UA has eight <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners (alumni and faculty), and more than 50 faculty as elected members of exclusive academies including <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Britain's Royal Society</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a>, among others. Two current UA professors were also recently named to <a href="/wiki/Popular_Science" title="Popular Science">Popular Science</a> magazine's list of &quot;Brilliant 10.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Highlights_and_rankings_15_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Highlights_and_rankings_15-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, well-known motion picture producer <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Bruckheimer" title="Jerry Bruckheimer">Jerry Bruckheimer</a> attended the University, receiving a degree in psychology. Many other famous names attended the University, such as socialite <a href="/wiki/Kourtney_Kardashian" title="Kourtney Kardashian">Kourtney Kardashian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Today_(U.S._TV_program)" title="Today (U.S. TV program)">Today Show</a> co-anchor <a href="/wiki/Savannah_Guthrie" title="Savannah Guthrie">Savannah Guthrie</a>, Cleveland Cavaliers Forward <a href="/wiki/Luke_Walton" title="Luke Walton">Luke Walton</a>, NBA player <a href="/wiki/Richard_Jefferson" title="Richard Jefferson">Richard Jefferson</a>, current <a href="/wiki/Boston_Celtics" title="Boston Celtics">Boston Celtics</a> player <a href="/wiki/Jason_Terry" title="Jason Terry">Jason Terry</a>, Minnesota Timberwolves Derrick Williams.</p>
